DEATH IS NOTHING!                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               It does not count. I have only slipped away into the next room. Nothing has happened.  Everything remains exactly as it was. I am I, and you are you, and the old life that we lived so fondly together is untouched, unchanged. Whatever we were to each other, that we are still.  Call me by the old familiar name. Speak of me in the easy way which you always used. Put no difference into your tone. Wear no forced air of solemnity or sorrow.  Laugh as we always laughed at the little jokes that we enjoyed together. Play, smile, think of me, pray for me. Let my name be ever the household word that it always was. Let it be spoken without an effort, without the ghost of a shadow upon it.  Life means all that it ever meant. It is the same as it ever was. There is absolute and unbroken continuity. What is this death but a negligible accident?  Why should I be out of mind because I am out of sight? I am but waiting for you, for an interval, somewhere very near, just round the corner.  All is well. Nothing is hurt; nothing is lost. One brief moment and all will be as it was before. How we shall laugh at the trouble of parting when we meet again!  Henry Scott-Holland. "Death Is Nothing At All." Family Friend Poems, 2006.

Damn, what can I say.  First I would like to say well done Scotto and team on the film it was perfect, no one could have done a better job.  True professionals, and I'm sure you hear all the time about how wonderful you all are and yada yada.  But I want to tell you about how your films have changed my life,  how in 2012 I was a homeless druggy that had lost all the spark in my life and frankly didn't care if it ended.  Then you guys shut the bay bridge down and a bunch of other streets and landmarks throughout the city, I was lucky enough to catch Ken launch over that crest on Russian hill and I was blown away.  I had no idea who Ken or [HOONIGAN] were but after looking y'all up I was hooked.  You see I grew up racing and loved every second of it, but when I hit my teenage years it was a wrap.  That dream was over,  and so I spent the next 20 years living a miserable, pointless, depressing life. Reading about Ken and Ken's life and his success in business, and his late start as a professional racer and the success he had doing it clicked something in my brain and I felt like I wasnt to old to start racing again.  That I could do it if I really tried and worked at it,  so I got my s#@% together and 3 years later I bought a shifter kart and started racing at the local track.  I know I would still be some junkie nobody if you guys hadnt filmed gymkhana in SF that year.  Ken quickly became my hero. Feb. 2023 I was diagnosed with prostate cancer and eventually had to sell my kart and everything else to pay for medical bills but I havent given up like I would have before Gymkhana and #43. I will get a new setup someday hopefully, but I want to say Thank you [HOONIGAN] and KB.  you are forever my hero.

10 years ago I was working in the drifting industry. Whenever I'd tell people about my job, they would ask: Oh, like Ken Block right? It annoyed me at first, but then I realized how many people had become interested in motorsports after seeing Ken and videos.
